   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiceless postalveolar fricative
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless" title="Voiceless">
        Voiceless
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fricative" title="Fricative">
        fricatives
       </a>
       produced in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postalveolar" title="Postalveolar">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       region include the voiceless palato-alveolar fricative
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       , the voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant fricative
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɹ̠̊˔]
       </span>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_fricative" title="Voiceless retroflex fricative">
        voiceless retroflex fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʂ]
       </span>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal fricative">
        voiceless alveolo-palatal fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɕ]
       </span>
       . This article discusses the first two.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

       </span>

      <p>
       A
       <b>
        voiceless palato-alveolar fricative
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        voiceless domed postalveolar fricative
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in many
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       , including English. In English, it is usually spelled ⟨sh⟩, as in
       <i>
        ship
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palatoalveolar_fricative.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="332" data-file-width="644" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Palatoalveolar_fricative.png/220px-Palatoalveolar_fricative.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Palatoalveolar_fricative.png/330px-Palatoalveolar_fricative.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Palatoalveolar_fricative.png/440px-Palatoalveolar_fricative.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palatoalveolar_fricative.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Postalveolar fricative
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʃ, ʒ]
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents this sound is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʃ
       </span>
       ⟩, the letter
       <a href="/wiki/Esh_(letter)" title="Esh (letter)">
        esh
       </a>
       introduced by
       <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Pitman" title="Isaac Pitman">
        Isaac Pitman
       </a>
       (not to be confused with the
       <a href="/wiki/Integral_symbol" title="Integral symbol">
        integral symbol
       </a>
       ⟨∫⟩). The equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        S
       </code>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       An alternative symbol is ⟨
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0" title="Š">
        š
       </a>
       ⟩, an
       <i>
        s
       </i>
       with a
       <a href="/wiki/Caron" title="Caron">
        caron
       </a>
       or
       <i>
        háček
       </i>
       , which is used in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americanist_phonetic_notation" title="Americanist phonetic notation">
        Americanist phonetic notation
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Uralic_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Uralic Phonetic Alphabet">
        Uralic Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       , as well as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_transliteration_of_Cyrillic" title="Scientific transliteration of Cyrillic">
        scientific
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/ISO_9" title="ISO 9">
        ISO 9
       </a>
       transliterations of Cyrillic. It originated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_orthography" title="Czech orthography">
        Czech orthography
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Jan_Hus" title="Jan Hus">
        Jan Hus
       </a>
       and was adopted in
       <a href="/wiki/Gaj%27s_Latin_alphabet" title="Gaj's Latin alphabet">
        Gaj's Latin alphabet
       </a>
       and other Latin alphabets of Slavic languages. It also features in the orthographies of many Baltic, Finno-Lappic, North American and African languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the voiceless palato-alveolar fricative:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">
         sibilant
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
         fricative
        </a>
        , which means it is generally produced by channeling air flow along a
        <a href="/wiki/Sulcalization" title="Sulcalization">
         groove
        </a>
        in the back of the tongue up to the place of articulation, at which point it is focused against the sharp edge of the nearly clenched teeth, causing high-frequency
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulence
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Palato-alveolar_consonant" title="Palato-alveolar consonant">
          palato-alveolar
         </a>
        </i>
        , that is, domed (partially
        <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">
         palatalized
        </a>
        )
        <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
         postalveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the blade of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        behind the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        , and the front of the tongue bunched up ("domed") at the
        <a href="/wiki/Palate" title="Palate">
         palate
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

         </span>

         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_sibilant" title="Voiceless retroflex sibilant">

            <b>
             ş
            </b>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ɟyˈne̞ʃ]
         </span>
        </td>

         'sun'
        </td>
        <td>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Turkish_phonology" title="Turkish phonology">
          Turkish phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Southern dialects
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="cy">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_alphabet" title="Welsh alphabet">
            mi
            <b>
             s
            </b>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>

          [miːʃ]
         </span>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="fy">
           <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">
            <b>

            </b>
            ippe
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>

       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Lombard_dialect" title="Western Lombard dialect">

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>

          Canzés
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="lmo">
           fe
           <b>
            sci
           </b>
           a
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>

          [feʃa]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'nuisance'
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">
          Yiddish
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span lang="yi">
          <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_alphabet" title="Hebrew alphabet">
           וויסנ
           <b>
            ש
           </b>
           אַפֿטלעכע
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [vɪsn̩ʃaftləxə]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'scientific'
        </td>
        <td>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Yiddish_phonology" title="Yiddish phonology">
          Yiddish phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">
          Yorùbá
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="yo">
           <b>
            ṣ
           </b>
           i
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʃi]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'open'
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_languages" title="Zapotec languages">
          Zapotec languages
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Tilquiapan_Zapotec" title="Tilquiapan Zapotec">
          Tilquiapan
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMerrill2008108_22-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMerrill2008108-22">
           [22]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="zts">
           <b>
            x
           </b>
           ana
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʃana]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'how?'
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In various languages, including English and French, it may have simultaneous
       <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">
        labialization
       </a>
       , i.e.
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃʷ]
       </span>
       , although this is usually not transcribed.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_spelling_and_pronunciation" title="Latin spelling and pronunciation">
        Classical Latin
       </a>
       did not have
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       , though it does occur in most
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       . For example, ⟨ch⟩ in French
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         chanteur
        </span>
       </i>
       "singer" is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       .
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         Chanteur
        </span>
       </i>
       is descended from Latin
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         cantare
        </span>
       </i>
       , where ⟨c⟩ was pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /k/
       </span>
       . The ⟨sc⟩ in Latin
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         scientia
        </span>
       </i>
       "science" was pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       , but has shifted to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       in Italian
       <i>
        <span lang="it">
         scienza
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Similarly,
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">
        Proto-Germanic
       </a>
       had neither
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       nor
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_fricative" title="Voiceless retroflex fricative">
         ʂ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , yet many of its descendants do. In most cases, this
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʂ]
       </span>
       descends from a Proto-Germanic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       . For instance, Proto-Germanic *skipą ("hollow object, water-borne vessel larger than a boat") was pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈski.pɑ̃/
       </span>
       . The English word "ship"
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃɪp/
       </span>
       has been pronounced without the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       the longest, the word being descended from
       <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">
        Old English
       </a>
       "
       <i>
        <span lang="ang">
         scip
        </span>
       </i>
       "
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃip/
       </span>
       , which already also had the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       , though the Old English spelling etymologically indicated that the old
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       had once been present.
      </p>
      <p>
       This change took longer to catch on in West Germanic languages other than Old English, though it eventually did. The second West Germanic language to undergo this sound shift was
       <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">
        Old High German
       </a>
       . In fact, it has been argued that Old High German's
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sk/
       </span>
       was actually already
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [s̠k]
       </span>
       , because a single
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
         s
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       had already shifted to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_apico-alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless apico-alveolar sibilant">
         s̠
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       . Furthermore, by
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_High_German" title="Middle High German">
        Middle High German
       </a>
       , that
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s̠k/
       </span>
       had shifted to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       . After High German, the shift most likely then occurred in Low Saxon. After Low Saxon, Middle Dutch began the shift, but it stopped shifting once it reached
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /sx/
       </span>
       , and has kept that pronunciation since. Then, most likely through influence from German and Low Saxon,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Frisian" title="North Frisian">
        North Frisian
       </a>
       experienced the shift.
      </p>
      <p>
       Then, Swedish quite swiftly underwent the shift, which resulted in the very uncommon
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Sj-sound" title="Sj-sound">
         ɧ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       phoneme, which, aside from Swedish, is only used in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colognian_language" title="Colognian language">
        Colognian
       </a>
       , a variety of High German, though not as a replacement for the standard High German
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       but a coronalized
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ç/
       </span>
       . However, the exact realization of Swedish
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɧ/
       </span>
       varies considerably among dialects; for instance, in Northern dialects it tends to be realized as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_fricative" title="Voiceless retroflex fricative">
         ʂ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       . See
       <a href="/wiki/Sj-sound" title="Sj-sound">
        sj-sound
       </a>
       for more details. Finally, the last to undergo the shift was Norwegian, in which the result of the shift was
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The sound in
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       denoted by ⟨ш⟩ is commonly transcribed as a palato-alveolar fricative but is actually a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_sibilant" title="Voiceless retroflex sibilant">
        laminal retroflex fricative
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiceless_postalveolar_non-sibilant_fricative">
        Voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant fricative
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant fricative">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant fricative
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ɹ̠̊˔
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ɹ̝̊˗
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA_number" title="IPA number">
          IPA number
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         151 414 402A 429
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         Encoding
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
          X-SAMPA
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <code>
          r\_-_0_r
         </code>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant fricative
       </b>
       is a consonantal sound. As the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       does not have separate symbols for the post-alveolar consonants (the same symbol is used for all
       <a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">
        coronal
       </a>
       places of articulation that aren't
       <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">
        palatalized
       </a>
       ), this sound is usually transcribed ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɹ̠̊˔
       </span>
       ⟩ (
       <a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Retracted" title="Relative articulation">
        retracted
       </a>
       constricted voiceless
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɹ]
       </span>
       ). The equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        r\_-_0_r
       </code>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_2">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
         fricative
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by constricting air flow through a narrow channel at the place of articulation, causing
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulence
        </a>
        . However, it does not have the grooved tongue and directed airflow, or the high frequencies, of a sibilant.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
         postalveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue behind the alveolar ridge.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_2">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Occurrence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         Language
        </th>
        <th>
         Word
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          IPA
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         Meaning
        </th>
        <th>
         Notes
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
          English
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_English" title="Irish English">
          Irish
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ireland_23-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-ireland-23">
           [23]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span lang="en">
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">
            t
            <b>
             r
            </b>
            ee
           </a>
          </i>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [tɹ̠̊˔iː]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'tree'
        </td>
        <td>
         Realization of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         after word-initial
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /t/
         </span>
         , unless it is preceded by
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /s/
         </span>
         within the same syllable.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ireland_23-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-ireland-23">
           [23]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/English_phonology" title="English phonology">
          English phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">
          Received Pronunciation
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoach2004240–241_24-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoach2004240–241-24">
           [24]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span lang="en">
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">
            c
            <b>
             r
            </b>
            ew
           </a>
          </i>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [kɹ̠̊˔ʊu̯]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'crew'
        </td>
        <td>
         Only partially devoiced. It is a realization of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         after the word-initial fortis plosives
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /p, k/
         </span>
         , unless they are preceded by
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /s/
         </span>
         within the same syllable.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoach2004240_25-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoach2004240-25">
           [25]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/English_phonology" title="English phonology">
          English phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-11">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFGussenhovenAarts1999">
           Gussenhoven &amp; Aarts (1999
          </a>
          :156). The authors state that
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/
          </span>
          is "pre-palatal, articulated with the blade of the tongue against the post-alveolar place of articulation". This makes it unclear whether this sound is palato-alveolar (somewhat palatalized post-alveolar) or alveolo-palatal (strongly palatalized post-alveolar).
         </span>
        </li>

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+the+International+Phonetic+Association&amp;rft.atitle=Standard+Georgian&amp;rft.volume=36&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=255-64&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2FS0025100306002659&amp;rft.aulast=Shosted&amp;rft.aufirst=Ryan+K&amp;rft.au=Chikovani%2C+Vakhtang&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVoiceless+postalveolar+fricative">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         <cite class="citation" id="CITEREFSilva2003">
          Silva, Thaïs Cristófaro (2003),
          <i>
           Fonética e Fonologia do Português: Roteiro de Estudos e Guia de Exercícios
          </i>
          (7th ed.), São Paulo: Contexto,
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">

           85-7244-102-6
          </a>
         </cite>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Fon%C3%A9tica+e+Fonologia+do+Portugu%C3%AAs%3A+Roteiro+de+Estudos+e+Guia+de+Exerc%C3%ADcios&amp;rft.place=S%C3%A3o+Paulo&amp;rft.edition=7th&amp;rft.pub=Contexto&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=85-7244-102-6&amp;rft.aulast=Silva&amp;rft.aufirst=Tha%C3%AFs+Crist%C3%B3faro&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVoiceless+postalveolar+fricative">

                       <p>
                        Where symbols appear in pairs, the leftmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">
                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
                       </p>
